(1/16/2016 4:22:57 AM) :SemiViral!~semiviral@AAB4772B:F29EDCF5:78E7B430:IP PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :What exactly is a rasberry pi? Like a barebarebarebones computer?

(1/16/2016 4:28:50 AM) :the_real_avid!odroid@hide-54F07F04.evrt.wa.frontiernet.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :this one i got an extra board for all the i/o stuff to play with sensors, addressable leds, that sort of thing
(1/16/2016 4:28:57 AM) :the_real_avid!odroid@hide-54F07F04.evrt.wa.frontiernet.net QUIT :Quit: leaving
(1/16/2016 5:07:09 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :SemiViral: what is a computer?
(1/16/2016 5:09:06 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :most of a raspi is just an ARM SoC. crystal oscillator, some regulators, passives (resistors and capacitors), the physical hardware required to make an HDMI port work, an SD card slot...
(1/16/2016 5:09:06 PM) :wally!~Jobot@ED24225B.F250ED5C.B92B1BFF.IP PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vWz9VN40nCA
(1/16/2016 5:09:24 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :and a built-in hardwired USB peripheral that has a hub and ethernet controller built-in
(1/16/2016 5:12:12 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :the audio port is a low-pass filter on two PWM outputs, the composite video generator's a part of the SoC, the SD card controller is on the SoC, RAM is off-die but stacked directly on top of the SoC iirc ("package on package")
(1/16/2016 5:12:38 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :so what is a raspi in the technical sense? it's the bare minimum amount of stuff added to an ARM SoC to make it usable.
(1/16/2016 5:13:53 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :everything that makes it "a computer" is broadcom's deal, built on the architecture (and probably also silicon) developed by ARM holdings from the original design by Acorn computers.
(1/16/2016 5:14:42 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :(with contributions from other licensees over time, from Apple to Intel to Marvell)
(1/16/2016 5:14:43 PM) :wally!~Jobot@ED24225B.F250ED5C.B92B1BFF.IP PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :All new Macbook Wheel, a revolution in computing simplicity.
(1/16/2016 5:16:42 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :most of the same goes for the massive flood of other SBCs (single-board computers) that followed the raspi into the consumer market, and many of the SBCs before that as well.
(1/16/2016 5:17:15 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :there are SBCs that effective implement everything a PC motherboard does, handle the support of a standalone CPU, and bring a bunch of complex components together...
(1/16/2016 5:17:47 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :and then there are SBCs built around an SoC that needs barely anything more than the appropriate voltages to become a computer
(1/16/2016 5:21:07 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :which is not to say it's a minimal-effort thing, configuring peripherals is always, erm, fun, and nothing something I'd expect the average joe to ever handle... but more and more peripherals are being tightly coupled into SoCs to the extent that addons and peripherals often just mean a physical connector being run to the correct pins.
(1/16/2016 5:24:02 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :decent audio, display, battery controller, wifi, bluetooth, infrared, and quality network interfacing generally need external devices though :p
(1/16/2016 5:26:29 PM) :jercos!jercos@hide-DC0A82D1.bic-son.net PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :(and the raspi has... none of these, while the ODROID-XU4 gains passable network support by using a USB 3.0 ethernet controller)
(1/16/2016 7:17:25 PM) :avid!~dulrich@F68B9C71.76BA63B6.5A483A0F.IP PRIVMSG #ministryofsillywalks :are you saying that the network on the XU4 is routed through a USB 3 ethernet controller?
